\nto the impacts of  climate change.', 'Objective 3: To help businesses and industries in the sector to access \nskills, training, knowledge and tools to understand and manage climate \nchange risks.', 'Objective 4: To ensure that investors and developers have the financial \nand appraisal decision tools needed to support and promote adaptation to \nclimate change.', 'Objective 5: To increase the resilience of  homes and buildings by helping \npeople and communities to understand what a changing climate could mean \nfor them and to take action to be resilient to climate risks.', 'Objective 6: To explore and build understanding of  the long term \nimplications of  climate change for the location and resilience of  population \ncentres.', 'Infrastructure Objective 7: To ensure infrastructure is located, planned, designed and \nmaintained to be resilient to climate change, including increasingly extreme \nweather events.', 'Objective 9: To better understand the particular vulnerabilities facing local \ninfrastructure (e.g. local highways) from extreme weather and long term \nclimate change so as to determine actions to address the risks.', 'Objective 10: To develop understanding and promote expertise in \nmanaging interconnected and interdependent services to minimise the risks \nof  cascade failures which could be exacerbated by climate change; and \nidentify how systems thinking can support this.', 'Uncertainty  Situation where the current state of  knowledge is such that (1) the order or nature \nof  things is unknown, (2) the consequences, extent, or magnitude of  circumstances, conditions, or \nevents is unpredictable, and (3) credible probabilities to possible outcomes cannot be assigned.', 'Vulnerability  the degree to which an individual or a system is susceptible to adverse effects. In this \ncontext, the adverse effects of  climate change, including extreme events. Vulnerability is influenced by \nthe systems sensitivity and its adaptive capacity, as well as the magnitude of  the change.', 'As required under Paragraph 58, Part 4 of  the Climate Change Act 2008 (c.27), this document \npresents: (a) the objectives of  Her Majestys Government in relation to adaptation to climate \nchange; (b) the Governments proposals and policies for meeting those objectives; and (c) the \ntime-scales for introducing those proposals and policies addressing the risks identified in the most \nrecent climate change risk assessment, as at July 2013.', 'Built Environment Objective 1: To work with individuals, communities and organisations to \nreduce the threat of  flooding and coastal erosion, including that resulting \nfrom climate change, by understanding the risks of  flooding and coastal \nerosion, working together to put in place long-term plans to manage these \nrisks and making sure that other plans take account of  them.', 'Objective 2: To provide a clear local planning framework to enable all \nparticipants in the planning system to deliver sustainable new development, \nincluding infrastructure, that minimises vulnerability and provides resilience \nto the impacts of  climate change.', 'Objective 3: To help businesses and industries in the sector to access \nskills, training, knowledge and tools to understand and manage climate \nchange risks.', 'Objective 4: To ensure that investors and developers have the financial \nand appraisal decision tools needed to support and promote adaptation to \nclimate change.', 'Objective 5: To increase the resilience of  homes and buildings by helping \npeople and communities to understand what a changing climate could mean \nfor them and to take action to be resilient to climate risks.', 'Objective 6: To explore and build understanding of  the long term \nimplications of  climate change for the location and resilience of  population \ncentres.', 'Infrastructure Objective 7: To ensure infrastructure is located, planned, designed and \nmaintained to be resilient to climate change, including increasingly extreme \nweather events.', 'Objective 9: To better understand the particular vulnerabilities facing local \ninfrastructure (e.g. local highways) from extreme weather and long term \nclimate change so as to determine actions to address the risks.', 'Objective 10: To develop understanding and promote expertise in \nmanaging interconnected and interdependent services to minimise the risks \nof  cascade failures which could be exacerbated by climate change; and \nidentify how systems thinking can support this.', 'Objective 19: To build the resilience of  wildlife, habitats and ecosystems \n(terrestrial, freshwater, marine and coastal) to climate change, so as to \nput our natural environment in the strongest possible position to meet the \nchallenges and changes ahead.', 'Objective 21: To promote and gain widespread uptake in other sectors of  \nthe use of  adaptation measures that benefit and/or do not adversely affect \nthe natural environment.', 'Objective 22: To improve the evidence base, to enhance the knowledge \nand understanding of  decision makers, land managers and others of  the \nimpacts of  climate change on the natural environment and how best we can \ninfluence adaptation or accommodate change.', 'Objective 24: To increase the extent to which businesses are actively \nconsidering climate change impacts, in their risk management and resilience \nplanning and decision-making processes, and taking appropriate adaptive action.', 'Objective 27: To undertake research to increase the understanding of  \nclimate change impacts on growth and the economy, working with investors, \ninsurers and other industry partners.', 'Objective 28: To raise and maintain the profile of  adaptation with local \nauthorities and promote action to embed climate resilience across local \nauthority services and responsibilities.', 'Objective 29: To support local government to build a credible business case \nfor action and take well-informed decisions both internally across service \nareas and externally with their local communities and businesses.', 'Objective 30: To ensure the policy framework for local government supports \ncouncils to increase community resilience in partnership with local and \nregional players.', 'Objective 31: To support sector-led activities, which allow councils to \nmake local commitments to address their own unique challenges and \nopportunities arising from changing climate.', 'Health Objective 11: To reduce the risk of  death and illness associated with \nsevere weather events and climate change and increase preparedness and \nresilience to the impacts on public health.', 'Objective 12: To promote climate resilience within the NHS, public health \nand social care system to ensure continuity of  services and resilient assets/\nestates including the ability to deal with the increased demand for services \nassociated with severe weather related events.', 'Objective 13: To minimise the impact of  climate change on vulnerable \ngroups in society by strengthening their resilience to better prepare for, \nrespond to and recover from future climate risk.', 'Objective 14: To promote and strengthen community resilience to severe \nweather related events linked to climate change (preparation, response and \nrecovery) and the climate resilience of  the emergency services and other \nCategory 1&2 Responders of  the Local Resilience Forums (LRFs).', 'Objective 15: To increase the resilience of  agriculture by effectively \nmanaging the impact of  volatility in the occurrence and severity of  rainfall \nevents on water availability, flooding, soil erosion and pollution due to runoff.', 'Objective 16: To increase the resilience of  the forestry sector by increasing \nthe level of  management in Englands woodlands and the uptake of  \nadaptation good practice in woodland creation and restocking.', "Objective 17: To increase resilience to pests and disease to help protect \nbiodiversity, maintain agricultural and forestry productivity and protect
